After I have finished your book of surgery and its supplementary material concerning the culmination point in medical science through Albucasis' eyes as well as their declarations about it, all has been done to complete this very tract on operations with hand (i.e., chirurgery).
Since the operation with hand (chirurgery) is established in our land and at this time alone: until perhaps it perishes as a science due to lack of study; its examination ceases altogether: so that nothing remains from those times except some incomplete descriptions found among ancient books, which had been corrected by hands—and errors occurred because they did not know the subject well enough. Thus has been explained this very tract on operations with hand (i.e., surgery), and I will complete it in accordance to my time of life: so that we may learn together from these words following formulated thoughts, abbreviations; when coming at last unitedly for cauterizing burns or treating wounds using remaining tools—based on what has been said regarding this subject by Albucasis.
Because for the reason that at this time not a good artist of hand (surgery) is found to accompany his art with it in our age: as surgery itself has grown long and requires an author well-versed in physiology, which Galenus narrated until he knew exactly how each member works—including its forms, connections, separations; also understanding of the bones, muscles, and blood vessels (and their number), and exits from them as to outward things.

I say therefore that the speech concerning the quality of cautery and its harm is a lengthy, subtle science, which is hidden knowledge.
Also spoken was there among the learned many on it, and they argued about it: and to me indeed suffices little from their speeches; I fear lengthening of discourse.
I say therefore that cautery furnishes universally for all kinds of illnesses which are with material and without: excepting two cases - hot sickness notwithterminal nor cold; a dry heat not terminal neither absent from the matter, and a likewise cool one.
Moreover in heated-cold with or without material they also disagreed. Some indeed said that cautery is suitable for those things as well. And others opposed them in this way; namely that cautery is not suitable for illnesses which are from hot and dry conditions: because nature itself is heat - as the saying goes 'nature abhorrs a vacuum'; so it follows-that being healed of such an affliction, made worse by warmth or drought (and this despite its own natural tendency to be relieved in these ways), can not truly recover health.
And he who said the contrary thereof; namely that by cautery is done iuvenation for all illnesses which are hot and dry-which happen to our bodies: when you compare body of man with its humours, if it be compared in relation to heat - then likened will you find his natural state cold.
And I, indeed, affirm by the speech of him himself; for he has already left that matter to me some times over.
Nevertheless it would be unsuitable for that matter to come before me unless he who has now already proven himself and is practised in the art of cauterization (and knowing well both differences among human complexions as regards disease, illness itself within us, causes thereof, consequences therefrom-accidents too - space also), all which I have previously spoken.
At those points then his fear for bodily wounds is not felt at all, especially with regard to colds and dampness. Indeed, all physicians agreed upon this matter, especially regarding the cautery; and they did not disagree with its use therein.
And he knew his son' endured treatment by Cautery with fire and that its quality over the burning medicine was good; for it is simple in action which does not arrive at body unless applied to a part cauterised: but hurts other members only if done unto the skin.
The burning action of medicine certainly reached this point that it extends from the members; and perhaps even causes death to occur at difficult diseases: probably kills.
Fire therefore because of its subtlety and goodness does not do this unless it is in excess.
Indeed now we realize that this was due to the weakness of our instruments and studies in medicine; and being situated over the truths of things, thus causing us to be excluded from such lengthy discourses about fire as are unnecessary for its use hereinabove mentioned: therefore excused by it.
And if not for the fact that this book does not permit me to discover from fire within it an occult secret; and its quality of operation in expelling diseases is as shown by philosophy's learned demonstration which will quiet philosophical minds, I would bring you back what has been concealed thus far.
And he knew his son that they themselves disagree about the time when it is convenient to perform Cautery; and preferring better times for speaking let this be left then as before mentioned hereinabove: therefore excused by its lengthiness also, because of which reason we have not yet said anything else.
I declare that Cautery is suitable at all times; because the harm resulting from it due to its being immersed comes into agreement with what has been said before mentioned hereinabove: therefore excused by this lengthiness too, as well for which reason we have not yet added anything else. Especially if the cauterium is due to painful conditions necessary for medical reasons, urgency or haste: therefore that it happens which may be a greater harm than mere physical injury because of time.
But let it not fall into the minds of those who are unconvinced unless they consult foolish or ignorant physicians: and mark this consequence, which is different from what people think: for that cauterium does not occur except in places related to medicine, since one thing alters complexion and another removes humidity, which are causes of pain.
But then the operation exceeds medicine and virtue of itself, and with earnest command from its master: and it is possible that he returns to health for some time according to the condition of his body, the location of disease, and his character or virtues: and what prepared within him comes out into this in food and drink (and other things like causes), unless a sickness arises which requires cauterium.
A sickness of delicate nature arises under slight inflammation and humidity, like the pain caused by cauterium used for teeth: it is possible that he does not return to health from this suffering. But such things are of short duration.
But truly there is another time to speak about this thing which the knife is at last medicine and not harm: for they believe that it does no healing or aid given by medicine itself with its own treatment nor after other treatments like incision have been done, contrary to what people intend in saying such things.
But on the contrary to this opinion is that which I have said before: and it has an aim not unless when we administer modes of cure in some disease, and do not give them any medical treatment: then finally we treat with medicine itself, and confer: so at last falls what was called post-remedies by physicians. Thus the knife is considered as a final resort for healing only after all other methods have failed to produce their desired effects on people considering such things foolish or absurd utterances of ignorant rhetoricals in medicine, and multistolid wicked doctors who understand nothing but how much harm they cause.
They said that the scalpel with gold is better than one with iron and they did not say so except for its equality to silver and solidity of substance itself; and they claimed it does not produce a place where abscesses form. But that is not true: for I have already tried it and found that this does not make such things without others in some corpses.
And they said the scalpel with silver is good itself and better than iron for it as well. But when you use fire for the scalpel in silver taken from gold as they say is good and better than iron itself; it does not declare to me that which happens if I light according to amount of fuel used because of tarnishing with gold: And, being suitable for coldness once ignited upon a wound over an incision by burning metal (as was done), liquefies in fire and rolls into layers.
Why does the artist fall from this into employment? And because of that reason it is fitting for a scalpel with iron to be used at our place and more suitable in respect to honesty towards operations.
And I have already arranged this chapter on the scalpel according to chapters for times sake, and from head to foot as in books till those seeking ask of that which they will do with it: so ordering shall be done towards them desiring knowledge about such things..

Head eighty.
Concerning the treatment of fistulas occurring in the lower part.
Fistulas occurring in the lower parts are nodulosis and enlargement that occur near ground level or at a certain height within a given space; they are one kind of fistula, but there can be more kinds.
So it must then that such old nodulosis opens and runs out of the wetness with white water or faint pus.

And it is known as fistula penetrating up to the navel; and even if there isn't such piercing through which passage exists from an intact or open one - for instance inserting your own finger into a belly button – when not tortuous, it can be inserted with fine wires made of metal.

And if you do not feel that way forthrightly - nor does any substance come out with evacuation or drainage as I have described; neither by urination nor through a discharge, and certainly no pus is produced – then you know this is non-penetrant: accordingly it should be directed to cure.
And when a fistula is penetrating until it reaches the urethra or bladder: then that signifies an outflow of urine from there and its prevention by this so as to solidify the location with medicine.
If it is penetrating as far as the hipbone or pubic bone: then that signifies a tract reaching up to there and continuing straight until not being entangled within its tortuous pathway unless towards the navel; when pain appears around this part, which ever emerges pus always without fail from it forevermore in need of medical treatment neither can solidify with ointment.

On treating displacement of fingers (Digitorum).
When the finger gets displaced out of its usual position either towards the back or on one side; then extend that digit and pull to restore its original alignment until it comes back in place: while doing this apply pressure over your thumbs as well for better effectiveness, allowing time only when they are safely returned.
Then afterwards support the head of the finger that is out of place and hold it under which side it has been displaced until they are securely fixed after two days; when this period ends release them for further treatment to ensure full recovery, without applying any pressure or restriction during sleep.
